# Introduction To Career Skills In Data Analytics

> Are you ready to take the first step on your journey as a data analyst? Whatever your goals, you don’t need a background in computer science to get started today. In this course, instructor Robin Hunt gives you a comprehensive, behind-the-scenes look at what it’s really like to be a data analyst, from wielding data concepts and business intelligence skills, to landing your first role and advancing

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics)
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

## Table of Contents

### Introduction

#### Starting out with data analytics
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=0)** - You are analyzing data all the time, from your step count to your bank account to whether your time is best spent cooking dinner or ordering out.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=9)** What I've discovered in the last 20 years is that more people use data than they even realize.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=14)** When I started off learning Excel, I had no idea I was starting my career path to data.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=19)** I quickly discovered that I could create reports that provided value to my managers.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=24)** But what I did not know is that I was providing critical information that would help drive the business.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=29)** Once I learned that I was seeing the world through a data lens, it provided me an opportunity to advance my career.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=35)** I could see data that others may have been missing and I could bring data sets together that others didn't believe possible.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=42)** I know firsthand when you invest in yourself, deepen your skills and understanding, it can be a game changer and totally change the trajectory of your career and the organization you serve.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=53)** Data has a profound impact on our everyday life as people and organizations.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=58)** It provides an opportunity for a generation that is already tech savvy but has an interest in business an opportunity to pursue one of the most valuable areas of business, data.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=69)** I'm Robin Hunt, co-founder of ThinkData Solutions, and I see data in everything.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=74)** I have worked with thousands of people to help them make data their next play.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=78)** You already have valuable context as to how data can make a difference, you just need to refine your skills.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/starting-out-with-data-analytics?u=76281980&t=84)** If you're ready to learn more about a career in data analytics, let's jump in and get started.

### 1. Introduction to Data and Data Analysis

#### Defining data analysis and roles in data analysis
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=1)** - One of the challenges we face as we decide to pursue data as a career choice is the fact that there are many different paths and specializations.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=8)** Let's define some of those roles, and then discuss the common skills that are shared among all.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=13)** The most universal role is that of the data worker.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=16)** This person consumes data regularly.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=18)** Works with data often.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=20)** Performs some data manipulation, and presents that data as a part of their everyday work.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=25)** Let's take Sally for an example.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=27)** She works in the business unit, and not necessarily the IT department, and each week she prepares a report for her manager.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=34)** She'll then prepare the data for the reports, and her reports are the same as last week, the only difference is new data.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=41)** You see most data workers have limited access to all the different systems through the backend.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=46)** They likely receive data from people who have access to the databases.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=50)** Data workers like Sally may even export the data out of a system into CSV or Excel files, and the process of their data work begins.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=59)** A data analyst goes further.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=61)** Generally, they might have a little more access to data, model the data, and have connected to the data, so they can just refresh the reports, and begin the analysis, and the presentation of the data.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=72)** The data analyst will handle a lot of ad hoc requests, and especially if they're efficient.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=78)** They will likely have more than just Excel to work with and are likely considered a guru or a wizard in their department.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=85)** The data worker and the data analyst are what I consider the largest amount of roles available.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=90)** Most people are some form of data worker, and they dive into data analysis more than they even know.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=96)** The common skills of all data professionals are gathering data.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=100)** manipulating it to me requirements, and then reporting the outcomes in some way.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=106)** Data engineers take a special skill of being able to build and design data sets.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=111)** Whereas a data worker, and the data analysts will work with what is already built, and model the data as needed.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=118)** You will find a lot of people in crossover roles where sometimes they play data engineers, and sometimes they act as a data analyst.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=126)** One could argue on the top of the hierarchy of data roles are the data architect, and the data scientist.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=132)** A data architect is a creator of architecture, no different than an architect that designs a building.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=138)** The data architect designs data systems.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=141)** The importance of the architecture really can't be understated as all roles including the data scientist needs this architecture.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=149)** What most see as the literal top of the hierarchy is the data scientist.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=154)** And I believe this is likely due to the fact that most companies have their data architecture in place, and now it's time to take that data, and put it to use.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=163)** This is where the data scientist comes into play.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=166)** A data scientist will likely have all the common skills of the data analyst, the data engineer and the data architect.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=173)** They'll also have deeper skills in coding, statistics and math.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=178)** It's okay to not know where you'll end on your journey, but I think it's important to start.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=184)** You can begin either as a data worker or recognizing you already are one.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=189)** You can increase your skills as a data analyst, and then as you grow deeper in your experience with data, you'll discover where you want to be.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/defining-data-analysis-and-roles-in-data-analysis?u=76281980&t=197)** In all roles, you'll gain a deeper understanding of data, and it's okay to find a place and stay there.

#### Developing data fluency
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=0)** - Is your organization data literate, data fluent, or none of the above?
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=5)** Let's break these terms down.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=6)** Data literate means that you could read it, converse about it, and understand it.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=11)** Let me give you an example, your bank account.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=14)** It's all about your finances, right?
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=16)** And if you really look at it, it's just all your data through transactions.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=21)** Can you read your balance?
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=22)** Can you tell me when something is there that shouldn't be?
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=25)** And if it is, can you call the bank and explain it?
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=28)** That means you're literate about your banking data.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=31)** Now to the meaning of fluent.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=33)** Fluent means you can create something with it that shows skills outside of just being able to read it and use it.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=39)** We know people who speak other languages.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=41)** They are either literate or fluent.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=44)** Someone who is literate can, again, pick up on the common things with the language and speak in simple sentences, but a person who is fluent can carry on conversations and author stories in that language.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=55)** Just like these terms apply to language, they apply to data.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=58)** Let's go back to our banking example.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=60)** If you are fluent with data, you can then turn your banking data from last year into insights that will allow you to build a budgeting system and a finance tracking system.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=71)** To really build your data skills, you must begin to think about how that data skill applies to your everyday life.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=76)** If you are data fluent, and at work someone hands you information, and it's the first time you've ever seen it, you will have an approach that lets you learn that data, and you will have questions that seem natural for you to ask.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=89)** Approach is everything, and building an approach or identifying it can start today, right now even.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=95)** Start thinking about every time you have a new data set in front of you, what do you do?
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=100)** That's your approach.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=101)** If your approach is to stare at it and wonder, well, that tells you where to begin.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=106)** Now there are degrees of data literacy and data fluency that are appropriate in the workplace.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=111)** And I would argue that everyone should be data literate.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=114)** The ability to read, speak, listen, and understand the data, or at least the data that applies to them.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=120)** Could be time sheets or even paychecks.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=124)** An organization that only has a small percentage of data fluent people means they do not have enough people to do the exploring and building that might just be the tool that takes their company to the next level.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=136)** Becoming data literate and then transitioning to data fluent can be a game changer in your career.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/developing-data-fluency?u=76281980&t=141)** You can go from reading and basic understanding to producing insight and data tools for your organization or maybe for yourself.

#### Understanding how data governance impacts the data analyst
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980&t=0)** - Have you ever asked permission to gain access to data and been denied?
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980&t=5)** Have you ever asked for permissions and just been given global admin when all you needed was read permissions?
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980&t=11)** If so, then you've been a part of the data governance of the organization, or the lack of it.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980&t=16)** Data governance is a framework that incorporates strategies to create solid quality data, enable accountability, and provide transparency to the data in the organization.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980&t=27)** Data governance has processes, procedures, and people at various levels of the organization.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980&t=33)** It's meant to control every aspect of the data in the organization.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-how-data-governance-impacts-the-data-analyst?u=76281980&t=37)** Data governance can support quality of data, accountability, trust, and compliance.

### 2. Introduction to Business Intelligence

> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=106)** Let me make it practical.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=107)** And I'll use health as an example.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=110)** If you know your heart rate as an adult is supposed to be anywhere between 60 to 100 beats per minute and you watch it every day and suddenly you see it spike and stay elevated, it would indicate that something is happening to make your heart beat faster.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=124)** With a bit more information like tracking what you eat or drink, you can analyze this data and you notice that it's elevated when you drink a certain type of drink and it stays elevated for a couple of hours and then goes back down.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=138)** To make an adjustment, you can stop drinking that drink or reduce the amount of it.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=143)** Whatever the adjustment is, you make it, you then analyze your heart rate to determine the adjustment to see if it made a difference.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=151)** When you apply this concept to the overall health of business then you can easily determine what the heart rate of the business is.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=159)** And what are the items that impact it.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/what-is-bi-and-the-value-to-business?u=76281980&t=161)** This allows you to start to define the metrics that help you monitor the health of the business and provide business intelligence.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** make (5)
> **Definitions:** is a  (2), means that (1)
> **Analogies:** for example (1), just like (1)
> **Code Keywords:** let (1)
> **Env Vars:** kpi (1)

### 3. Identifying Data

#### Understanding the value of data-driven decision-making
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=0)** - If I told you that we have an opportunity to purchase a product, and that it was going to make a million dollars in the first year, you would get excited, right?
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=8)** That one number sounds amazing to people.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=11)** Some people would immediately look at that number and begin to act; that is a data-driven decision.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=17)** In our scenario, our company thought the product at cost was a steal of a deal, and they bought it all with the hopes that a million in revenue would produce a large profit.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=26)** The only problem is that million dollar number is only the top line and in no way reflects the impact to the bottom line.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=33)** When people get a single number in their mind, they can miss the other more important numbers, and it can have damaging consequences.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=40)** Let's take our million-dollar project and break it down.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=44)** The company bought the product at cost, and the company will sell the product at a list price, and the difference between that cost and the list price is the margin.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=53)** All the numbers here, cost, list and margin, matter but of the three, the margin matters the most.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=60)** It's important to remember that a million in revenue does not equal a million in profit.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=65)** Our profit is made by the margin.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=68)** Some people see that margin and get excited, but if you stop there, you are in trouble.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=72)** You must account for the items that eat the margin because that eats the profit.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=77)** When you use data to inform your decision making, you must use the top-down and bottom-up approach together.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=83)** If you're an experienced person with these types of scenarios, you may have already figured out where this is headed.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=88)** What do we need to do to produce the distribution of this product?
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=92)** We'll keep it simple.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=93)** When companies sell products, someone has to sell them and there's a cost to that.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=99)** And even if it's an online sales model, there are people involved in maintaining the information to make that happen.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=105)** Let's just say for every $1 of the product, it costs 10 cents of that dollar to pay for the sales process.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=111)** Then there are other costs: cost to store the product, cost to package the materials, cost to deliver the product.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=118)** There's cost in infrastructure.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=120)** Cost to automate sales processes.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=122)** Payroll costs for people to maintain systems, answer phones, and ensure that delivery is met.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=128)** If you really dig in, you realize quickly that if everything that is required to make the million in revenue eats up the entire margin, or you sold it at the wrong price, or you get hit with unexpected costs like increase in delivery, increase in storage or changes to tax, you are sunk.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=145)** And if you can't sell it and you can't hold onto it, that million dollars no longer looks like a gold mine.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/understanding-the-value-of-data-driven-decision-making?u=76281980&t=152)** So the impact of being data informed can ensure you're profitable, and that million dollars is really not a million dollars after all, but a total loss, which is maybe why it was a steal of a deal in the first place.

> **Code Keywords:** let (2)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)

#### Questioning techniques to collect the right data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - Have you ever heard of analysis paralysis?
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=3)** It's where you overthink a problem that stops you from moving forward.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=6)** It's a real thing for some people.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=8)** It's likely due to stress and anxiety related to making the wrong decision or not knowing exactly what to do next.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=15)** Building an approach and thinking through standard questions and critical thinking with active listening should help you.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=21)** Technical skills or hard skills are one thing for the analyst, but the soft skills matter just as much.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=27)** And if you're stuck, no hard skill matters.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=31)** To be fair, the more exposure to real problems and solving them with data solutions will help you build your approach, but you can slowly start building your questioning now.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=40)** There are some common questions you might ask for every data-related project and the questions might be more specific based on actual problems and the data that you have at hand.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=51)** Our scenario is that we have five of our top products.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=54)** They're being purchased all the time, but the company is losing money.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=58)** First, you need to understand that there is data in everything, in it and around it.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=63)** This will help you start to consider the questions.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=67)** Our task as the analyst is to try to determine why if the sales are moving, why are we losing?
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=73)** There are some basic questions that you should ask about each of the five products.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=78)** Have these products ever been profitable?
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=80)** If they were profitable in the past, at what point in time?
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=84)** What is different about this point in time versus that point in time?
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=88)** Did the wholesale cost change?
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=90)** Did the list price change?
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=92)** Did the cost of storing or delivering the product change?
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=96)** Any of these answers will lead you further into data analysis.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=100)** When we start with these basic questions and begin to answer them, then it will lead to more questions.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=107)** As an example, let's say that in our initial questioning, we determine that the wholesale costs nor the list price have changed in the last three years.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=116)** The cost to deliver has not changed enough to drive an impact.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=120)** The cost of storing the products has been steadily increasing.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=125)** The next round of questions begin.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=129)** Is it only these five products that are impacted by the steady increase of storage cost?
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=134)** And what we discover, it's not just impacting these five products but all the products.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=140)** The company just started to realize it in these five products.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=144)** What can we do to reduce the storage costs?
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=148)** What type of increase can we justify on the products without overpricing the product?
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=154)** Both these questions lead to very different datasets within the organization and then each round of questions and answers leads to more questions.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=165)** The goal here is to remember you must start asking questions and then remember they rarely stop.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=171)** They just drive further investigation.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/questioning-techniques-to-collect-the-right-data?u=76281980&t=175)** The greatest part of the question process is that the end result is discovery and recommendations that are made to improve outcomes.

> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/discovering-and-interpreting-existing-data?u=76281980&t=194)** Just remember data shows up in everything but it's our job to bring it together accurately.

#### Data sources and structures
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=0)** - We hear about data all the time, right?
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=2)** But what does that really mean?
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=4)** Let's start with the basics.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=6)** Data has a value, like your birthday, that's a value like November 20th of any year.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=12)** So your birthday would be 11/20 of that year.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=16)** Data has a type, like birthday. It's a date data type.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=22)** And data has a field name, like DOB, for Date of Birth.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=27)** When we put these fields together, like First Name, Last Name and Date of Birth, we're creating a record.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=34)** People use records and spreadsheets all the time, but they don't really think of the sheet as a table, but it actually is.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=41)** It's just a table called Sheet One.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=43)** And when fields are combined in a database, they're stored in tables.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=47)** They still have names, values, and data types.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=50)** And when we fill in this information for a person, we're creating a record.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=56)** Tables are a great way to capture multiple types of data in a structured way.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=61)** This way of storing data is way more flexible than the spreadsheet environment.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=66)** There are also other types of systems that collect and store data for the analysts to use for their reporting requirements.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=73)** This varies of course by company, but you can expect to find spreadsheets, databases or even data warehouses.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=81)** Data warehouses really are data systems that have the refined tables from our production systems, like the purchasing system, for example.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=89)** A customer-dedicated software system might have a database with hundreds of tables and details, but only certain tables and fields are needed for reporting.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=99)** These fields get cleaned up by data warehousing professionals and brought into the warehouse for storage and safekeeping.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=106)** It is a valuable source of nicely structured data that has been vetted for the analysts to begin their reporting projects.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=114)** Structured data that fits neatly into tables and feeds a beautifully designed warehouse is amazing, but not all data is structured.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=123)** This is where systems like data lakes help organizations capture data so they're storing it before it's actually refined for reporting needs.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=132)** Data warehousing and data lakes and even data lake houses are very interesting.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=137)** And if you're into designing databases or designing data solutions, you may find you want to explore these skills further.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=144)** Data analysts will tap into these systems for the data.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=148)** They don't necessarily create them.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=150)** As a data analyst, you will find yourself working with various systems and file types.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=156)** At the start of your career, you can expect a lot of spreadsheets and CSP files as you work your way up into working with data stored in larger data systems.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-sources-and-structures?u=76281980&t=165)** And don't worry, no matter the level, most data professionals love a good spreadsheet when it's used for analysis and not for storing data.

### 4. Preparing Data

#### Describing data best practices
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/describing-data-best-practices?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>

#### Transforming data in Power BI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/transforming-data-in-power-bi?u=76281980)

#### Common cleaning and transformation
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=0)** - When building your cleaning and transformation toolbox, there's some common cleaning and transformation items you will use.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=7)** Others will be more specific to the deeds of the data you work with.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=11)** Let's start with general cleaning.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=13)** Spaces are invisible to the eye, but in fact, they're characters.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=17)** And when a field has extra spaces, you will want to clean those by removing them.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=21)** There are leading spaces which are spaces that are at the front of the field.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=25)** There are trailing spaces which are at the end of the field.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=29)** When we want to remove either leading or trailing spaces, then we can use functions like trim or clean.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=35)** The act of breaking out text is referred to as parsing text.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=38)** And we can do this with any type of delimiter and every program handles this a little bit differently, but the outcome is the same.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=46)** Spaces will also serve as a delimiter, like the spaces between words are valid spaces.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=52)** Imagine first name and last name.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=54)** In the case we want to have both last and first in their own individual columns for sorting, as an example, we will use the space to break those columns.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=64)** This is not the only time we parse texts using delimiters.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=67)** You might break apart text fields based on things like a dash or even a comma.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=71)** We use things like text-to-columns, split by delimiter and functions like left, right and mid to work with parsing text.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=80)** We don't only break apart text.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=82)** There's also times when we need to combine text fields together.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=85)** This is commonly known as concatenate or concat.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=89)** We also replace text with valid text.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=91)** For example, if someone enters an abbreviation of a state in the United States, but we want the full state spelled out, we might replace that text with the valid response.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=101)** It could be a misspelling that we're correcting.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=104)** There are several methods for replacing invalid data with valid data.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=109)** We also change the case of text.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=111)** Example would be maybe we need everything to be in uppercase or lowercase or even corrected to proper case.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=118)** There are functions to do each of these commands, and again, they might differ between programs, but the outcome will be the same.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=125)** These are very simple commands to perform in any data program.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=130)** You may find that you'll also remove duplicates from a dataset and this can be done with commands like remove duplicates or using distinct keywords inquiry statements.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=140)** We also transform data types to be appropriate for what we need to do with the data.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=145)** You may have date fields that are stored as text, but to work with date-related functions, you need to convert it to an actual date data type.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=153)** The same goes for numbers.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=155)** If you need to work with a mathematical function, then the value of the field must be a number data type.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/common-cleaning-and-transformation?u=76281980&t=161)** These are just a few of the basic commands that we use for cleaning and transformation of data and some of the first ones to understand and master.

> **[7:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/using-built-in-functions?u=76281980&t=425)** I tell people all the time, anyone can make numbers show up, but that does not make them correct.
>
> **[7:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/using-built-in-functions?u=76281980&t=431)** If I could offer you a piece of advice, really think through what you're trying to accomplish with the numbers, consider what functions you might need and then also read about what's available.
>
> **[7:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/using-built-in-functions?u=76281980&t=442)** The more experience you have, the easier the research will be for you but don't worry, you'll always be studying something new.

### 6. Modeling Data

#### Relational databases
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=0)** - Have you ever really thought about how systems store data?
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=5)** I bet if you're a new analyst, you have not gotten that deep into the idea of how data is stored, but you just know that it is stored.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=12)** Relational databases have been around for a while and you will hear people talk about SQL databases or SQL scripts or statements.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=19)** A data analyst doesn't have to be fluent to be effective.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=23)** You can do a lot with just being somewhat literate with SQL.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=27)** This is a key area that you can further study if you're interested.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=31)** RDBMS stands for Relational Database Management Systems and server technology, like Microsoft SQL Server, can store these databases.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=40)** There are others.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=42)** Even something as simple as an Access database has relationships and relational data.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=48)** We need to go back one step and discuss structured data.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=51)** When you work with a spreadsheet that has column headings and data values, then you're actually working with structured data.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=58)** This data has a field name, we see it in the column headings, and then it has a data type and a value.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=64)** When we build relational databases, we build structured data sets that are stored in the form of tables.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=70)** These tables then become connected through a relationship between key fields.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=74)** These key fields are unique identifiers that help control the data that can and cannot go into a table.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=81)** When structured data is defined and then stored into tables and then the tables are related, this creates a relational database.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=89)** These relational databases are used to hold information and we as data analysts use this structured and stored data to build reports, visuals, and analyze data.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=100)** One thing that is important to note is that you as the data analyst must understand the structure that is used to store the data does not always make it easy for reporting.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=109)** Why?
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=110)** The rules for effective storage are different from the rules used to combine data for reporting.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=116)** They are two very distinct roles and functions, even if they work with the same data.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/relational-databases?u=76281980&t=121)** As an analyst, you do not have to know how to design large-scale data systems, but you will want to understand some database design techniques so that it makes understanding someone else's design easier.

#### Modeling data for Power BI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript

>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=6)** When we have multiple tables that we're working with, we'll want to model our data to get the most out of it.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=12)** When you have an entity relationship diagram where the tables and relationships are showing in a model, you're actually seeing the model of the data.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=21)** Now I've already connected data to my Power BI Desktop and on the right hand side, you see my fields list.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=27)** I have different tables of information required for my reporting.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=31)** It appears that I'm ready to go but I need to go one step further.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=36)** These data sets are meant to be joined together.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=40)** There are several ways to join and model data in Power Query for Power BI.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=45)** When we perform merge queries, for example, we're actually establishing a join but we can also go to the modeling section and model this data from the very beginning and this allows the data to communicate through the joins, meaning if I reference an order, it knows what product and what order details are related to that order.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=65)** In looking at the diagram, we see that there are some joins already established.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=70)** Power BI as a convenience tries to join the data automatically, this is called auto detect and it tries to auto detect the relationships.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=79)** You should always confirm that the relationships that it establishes for you are correct.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=85)** Remember, it's easy to model data when you know what data is related to each other.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=90)** Let's look at the orders table and the order details.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=93)** These are joined together by the order ID.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=96)** Also notice we have a '1' and a '*' or star symbol.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=102)** This shows us the cardinality of this relationship, it's a one to many, meaning we have one order and many order details, not unlike when you place an order and buy multiple things, you have one order record and then the different line items and quantities for the products that you purchased.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=122)** Let's look at the products information and the order details.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=127)** These are joined by the product ID and again, it's a one to many relationship.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=132)** There are other relationships when we refer to cardinality, there's one to many, many to one, one to one and many to many.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=143)** One to one means that there is only one record tied to one record between the two tables.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=149)** One to many and many to one, like our examples here mean that we have one record in one table that's tied to many records in another table.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=158)** I do have a join that needs to exist but doesn't.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=162)** Take a look at the employees, you see how there's no line to any other table, this means that the model doesn't know how the employees relate.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=171)** I'll use the employee ID and drag it to employee ID, this establishes my relationship.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/modeling-data-for-power-bi?u=76281980&t=180)** I can go ahead and look at the properties of this relationship.
