#### Master data management
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=0)** - Have you ever been working with data and you see customer addresses all have different ways to reference the region?
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=7)** In some countries, we have states, provinces, or districts.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=10)** And when they're used in the data and entered by different people, they may reference the full state, province, or district name or they may list the abbreviation.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=19)** Data like our customer and their address information would be considered master data.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=23)** We want everyone in the organization who works with this data to have the same consistent list of information.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=29)** When an organization takes the time to design rules around the master data, this will also inform all the data analysts of what types of transformations apply.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=38)** Using tools like Power Query, either in Excel or Power BI, we can easily make these corrections and save these steps so that as new data comes into our reports, it will conform to the standards.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=50)** Master data is not just address information, though.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=52)** It could be project names or product names.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=55)** If we call a project something different, then it makes it difficult for the data analyst to report on this information with ease.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=62)** There are tools that exist to support large scale organizations with master data management.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=67)** But I would argue no matter the size of your organization, if you do not have a plan in place, the analyst will be dealing with it all the time.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=75)** So as master data management aims to keep a clean, complete, and accurate list of master data for the organization, if you don't have master data management, then you will need to develop a plan to keep a nice, consistent list of data when you report.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=89)** Let's take products, as an example.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=92)** Two companies have merged.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=93)** They sell the exact same products, but in both companies, they're not called the same name.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=98)** As a data analyst, you can use a table that holds every possible name and the correct name so that when you report, you can leverage joints to give yourself a master table of information.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=108)** When a new name pops up, you'll have to address it in your master table, but it's better to have that table than to not have it.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=115)** Your data set being clean and complete is one of the most important parts of any project.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/master-data-management?u=76281980&t=121)** Just remember that all of your data skills can apply to many types of data scenarios, not just the analysis or the presentation part of the job.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Code Keywords:** let (1)
> **Speakers:** - have (1)

#### Unstructured data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - Did you know that there is way more unstructured data in the world than structured?
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=5)** As a matter of fact, did you know we use structured data to produce even more unstructured data?
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=11)** Data that neatly fits into tables or spreadsheets is structured data, and unstructured data is literally everything else.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=18)** When we post videos, take pictures, create PDFs of bills for our clients, we are contributing to the vast amount of constant unstructured data.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=28)** The minute we had the ability to walk around with a PC, video camera, still camera and social media outlets in our hands like our mobile devices, the world of data exploded.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=39)** Let's just take an image for example.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=41)** This is unstructured data.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=43)** You must look at the image to understand what the image is representing.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=47)** Same thing for a video.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=49)** You have to watch it, and it's an immense amount of data.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=53)** With that said, there's also semi-structured data, which is a mix of both structured data, and unstructured data.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=60)** Let's say you receive an image of the cutest cat ever on the beach via a text from your best friend.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=66)** When you see this image, you see the cutest cat ever or at least someone's opinion that is the cutest cat ever, and you see the beach.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=73)** A data professional sees much, much more.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=76)** What I see when I look at the cutest cat ever picture is much more than a cat in the beach.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=81)** I see the time of day, the weather, the location, the type of cat, the color of the cat, even the age of the cat.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=90)** I also see the image type like PNG, and what's the image size, as well as the dimensions, and what's the quality of the image.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=99)** Don't forget.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=100)** We mentioned that we received this from someone, that's data.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=103)** We received it at a certain time, and that's data.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=107)** Did I mention when the picture was taken, and by who?
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=110)** I mean this list can keep going.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=112)** Just think.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=113)** It went from being the cutest cat ever to a lot of data really fast.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=117)** Now, imagine people posting their favorite images on their social feeds.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=121)** Multiple times per minute, and then others are sharing that image or they like it, or they look at it and move on.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=128)** That's also data.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=130)** Unstructured data requires our brain to review and provide context, and structured data fits neatly into designs.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=136)** And semi-structured is everything in-between structured and unstructured.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=141)** Depending on the organization you work with, and what they do as their product or service will determine what tools, and software you need to work with with their data.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=150)** Just knowing that there are different types of data like structured and unstructured can help you explore the roles in data.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=156)** Data is not going anywhere.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=158)** It is only growing.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=160)** And just think, there was a time when the name didn't exist.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/unstructured-data?u=76281980&t=163)** It should keep us all motivated for what's coming next.

### 7. Visualizing Data

#### Visualization methods and best practices

>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=91)** If my brain says, "This product is blue on this stacked bar," then every time I see a reference to this product, it will be blue.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=99)** And then when I believe this new visual has the same blue, is the same item, and I realize it's a totally different product, I get stuck on why isn't this the same?
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=109)** And the data is not showing me anything.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=112)** Don't overcomplicate to show your fancy vis skills.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=116)** I do understand that people want to use advanced visuals to show their skills.

>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=126)** If you provide valuable insight through correct visuals and layout, they will believe you to be a visual magician, and they will not care that you presented it in simplified visuals.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=136)** Be sure to title, label, and add tooltips appropriately.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=140)** People should be able to read a title for context, be able to easily read the labels, and hover over to get additional insight, not just see the same thing the visual already shows.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=150)** Remember that a picture is worth a thousand words.

> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=153)** And if we could all make decisions by consuming thousands of lines of data, we wouldn't need visuals.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=159)** Not all data visualization is a chart or graph.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=162)** Make appropriate use of cards for high level totals and other aggregate functions.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=167)** And remember, a table, matrix or pivot is also a visual presentation of data, and some people prefer that matrix to a chart.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=175)** So it never hurts to give them both to meet the needs of the audience.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=179)** Always remember that your visuals will be used to provide information.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/visualization-methods-and-best-practices?u=76281980&t=183)** So make sure that it does it in a way that people can quickly understand and make decisions.

> **[8:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/creating-a-dashboards-for-reporting?u=76281980&t=523)** When we take data from reading it line by line on multiple pages to being interactive, we're giving people the ability to question the data, create different scenarios and then also providing actionable insight.

#### Gathering requirements for visualizations
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=0)** - We have all heard the stories where the entrepreneur designs their life-changing app on a napkin and then moves on to greatness.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=7)** Well, guess what?
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=8)** You can apply the same approach to your visuals.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=11)** Maybe it's not a napkin, but I can tell you from my experience, even starting with your customer and a napkin is better than guessing at the visual representation of the data on your own.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=21)** People never know what they want in a dashboard or report until they can see what you see, and if that's all in your head, well no one is a mind reader.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=29)** The best way to express your ideas is to create a mockup of the dashboard.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=34)** Just lay out different objects, like a table, matrix or stack chart, add a few filters on the image, this will help everyone get on the same page about the design.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=44)** And if it's multiple pages with navigation, then wireframing helps communicate the navigation of information before you build it.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=52)** Wireframing allows you to build out a skeleton of the pages, it doesn't have to be designed with all the colors and final graphics, it's just a sketch.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=60)** The mockup might have a little more visual styling than the wireframe, but even just a few minutes of investing time into these together will reduce tons of back and forth on the design process.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=71)** There are many ways to produce mockups and wireframes, we can thank all the software developers and UX designers for these sets of tools.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=79)** If you are newer, it might be hard to visualize the visuals needed because you may still be trying to determine the right visual for the data.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=87)** You can look for inspiration through samples that you can find available in the software, like Power BI has a whole set of dashboards you can play around with to get started.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=96)** In addition to getting on the same page about the look of the dashboard, we must consider other requirements.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=102)** Be sure you're documenting these in every meeting and then following up with notes to all stakeholders afterwards.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=109)** A few items to always address are, what type of filters do we need on the data?
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=114)** That way you're not bringing in more than what's needed.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=117)** Example would be a 100 year old company doesn't need 100 years of data in the dashboard.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=123)** I would call this a hard filter, that's because you handle this type of filter at the data level.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=128)** What type of filters are needed for the consumer?
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=131)** Which is the user of the dashboard.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=133)** What might they search and filter?
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=135)** These are soft filters and they're meant to be interactive.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=139)** Common filters might be years and dates.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=142)** If it's dedicated to products, it will likely have a product filter.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=146)** And if it's dedicated to customers, it will have some customer filters.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=150)** Never fail to find out who this dashboard actually is for, and also determine if they have the permissions to the data and the correct licensing to use the dashboard.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=160)** Visualization is as much an art as it is a science, and these requirements are pretty standard to every type of visualization project.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/gathering-requirements-for-visualizations?u=76281980&t=168)** And you'll discover there are many more, but if you start with these, you'll be designing better dashboards right from the beginning.

#### Presenting data challenges effectively to others
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980)

>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=13)** That's tough.

>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=43)** It's a high stakes project.

>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=70)** What do you do facing this scenario?

>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=90)** People make mistakes.
>

>

>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=106)** And by the way, they may have a very sound reason for those gaps.

>

>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=117)** The organization is hoping that the data team will be able to show something very positive with the data, and you found the exact opposite to be true.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=126)** This is truly a challenging scenario and not a fun one to face.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=130)** So what do you do?
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=132)** When I find myself in this situation where there is a totally different understanding of the data reality versus the actual reality, I start by confirming that I'm not missing something.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=143)** I double check everything.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=145)** I confirm that I've not introduced an error in any way.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=149)** If I find that this is the truth of the data, then I turn to the person in leadership and discuss my findings to get further insight into what I may be missing and get guidance from them on the next steps for me to take.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=161)** Remember, we don't have access to all the data or even all the knowledge.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=166)** Turning to your leadership is the legitimate next step.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=170)** If you discover no errors, you have done all that you can have and the truth isn't going to be exactly what they planned.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=178)** Having some communication skills on how to deliver information might be your next step.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=184)** Remember, data is used to inform a business for improvement and sometimes delivering the results can be hard.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/presenting-data-challenges-effectively-to-others?u=76281980&t=191)** As a data professional, just make sure you have thoroughly checked all your results, follow the chain of command of information, and by all means, communicate with your team.

#### Finalizing dashboards
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/finalizing-dashboards?u=76281980)

### 8. Job Mapping in the Data Analytics Field

#### Data workers
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=0)** - If you use spreadsheets every day and you create valuable insights for people through various presentations or reporting, you are a data worker.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=8)** But you're not likely called that by your job title.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=11)** You may have a job title that represents a department or the people you support, but you're not titled data worker.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=17)** You just are one.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=19)** I would also consider you a data worker if you find yourself exporting data out of systems, building some form of report or presentation weekly or monthly.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=27)** You may also receive data from someone in another department, like IT, who has access to more data than you.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=33)** You may frequently visit the company's data warehouse, or data system, to gain information for your reporting purposes.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=39)** Data workers also work with functions and do some aggregate functions with the data.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=44)** You may use some logical functions like an if.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=48)** You're able to search for functions and find the ones that are relevant to your data work, you are likely a data worker.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=55)** I believe that there are far more data workers than our organization realize, and if you're in this role, guess what?
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=61)** You're a great resource.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=62)** And one of the first places an organization can turn to, to upscale and data.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=67)** If you're looking for areas of growth, then make sure you're using tools in Excel like Power Query and other analysis techniques like PivotTables and basic visualizations.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=77)** If you have more than average skill with these, you might be more than a data worker already.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=82)** You can also build skills like PowerPoint because this is another way we visualize data for meetings and presentations.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=88)** Documentation is a critical competency for any data role, so being a wizard at Microsoft Word doesn't hurt.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=95)** Remember, like every other tool, it's powerful and often because we use it every day, we don't believe we need to explore training.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=102)** Trust me, you should.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=104)** For the soft skills, you'll want to focus on effective presentations and communication skills.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-workers?u=76281980&t=109)** Having these skills make you more than suitable for roles that require advanced skills in Excel and doing basic analysis.

#### Data analysts
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=0)** - I have spent years trying to define data analysts to people.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=4)** I've come up with several ways to try to define this role and the skills.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=7)** It's important to know that mos, do not have a job title that contain the words data analyst, but if you have a data department, then they are likely to be called data analyst.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=17)** Not all organizations have a dedicated data department.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=21)** So you might be called an operations analyst or a marketing analyst.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=25)** Your title likely has analyst in the title.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=28)** There are also varying levels of data analyst, and you can be a data analyst, and not know it.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=34)** Or be performing the skills of an analyst, and have no idea that you are.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=38)** A data analyst will have a deeper understanding of data systems and have more knowledge about database designs than a data worker.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=45)** A data analyst will find they have a little more access to see tables, and views of the databases.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=51)** They probably have some basic SQL querying skills and may write SQL statements to gain access to data all the time.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=57)** This varies by organization, and access levels.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=61)** A data analyst will have a better than average understanding of the data governance plan because if you're a data analyst, you are going to be working under the policies, and procedures that are established.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=71)** Data analysts that are a few years in are likely to understand more about what questions to ask, and research in general.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=79)** Data analysts understand how to clean data, and transform it to meet the requirements of the project.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=84)** Data analysts also know how to create functions of varying types like conditional statements, logical statements.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=90)** Data analysts work with statistics, and most certainly at the beginning of their career, basic stats and aggregate functions, and certainly have learned how to connect data in a way that they can just refresh their data, and update their visuals and reports.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=106)** If you're looking for areas of growth, then you can go a little bit deeper into statistics.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=111)** It's a must.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=112)** Note that I said a little deeper, not a full statistician, which is another role entirely.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=118)** You'll find the data sets you are developing might be used for different statistical tests.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=123)** So it is important to have a basic knowledge.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=126)** You can never have enough experience writing functions, and you definitely want to be able to write if functions, aggregate functions and simple lookups.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=136)** You must understand joins, and how they impact data sets.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=140)** And for the soft skills, active listening, data storytelling, and critical thinking.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-analysts?u=76281980&t=146)** If you're realizing that you're a data analyst, then you might relate to being called a wizard at work.

>
> **CLI Commands:** find (2)
> **Env Vars:** sql (2)
> **Warnings:** note that (1)
> **Speakers:** - i (1)

#### Data engineers
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=0)** - It is one thing to refine and add to a data set.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=3)** It's an entirely different skill to be able to build data sets.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=8)** I personally believe what most people consider, as a data analyst in their organization, may be performing data engineering tasks more than analysis tasks.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=17)** The crossover between the analysts and the engineering and skills are real.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=21)** They share a lot of common foundational skills.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=24)** A data engineer is someone who fully understands how to look at the data sets, knows how to refine them into smaller more sensible sets for people to use.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=32)** You may receive data from someone who is engineering that data from a set of queries, and then providing it to you or others.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=40)** A data engineer also is likely to have more access to data, which is why they're sending it to you in the first place.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=46)** They also understand security and privacy of data through the overall data governance strategy.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=52)** Data engineers can transition to data architect, which covers more systems, more server and more security strategies for systems across all of the organization.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=61)** If you want to grow further in this role, you will certainly need to understand more about structured and unstructured data and how to convert it to usable data sets.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=70)** You'll want to understand the design methodologies of relational database systems and you will need to understand how to design databases.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=78)** You'll also want the shared skills of communication, effective presentations, critical thinking, and active listening.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=84)** These skills will be used to learn how to take hundreds of tables to define them into usable tables for other processes using ETL or ELT, which is extract, transform, and load or extract, load, and transform.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=98)** This is how data goes from a production system to a data warehouse, as an example.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-engineers?u=76281980&t=103)** I believe there is a lot of opportunity for data analysts to pursue this role as they grow deeper in their understanding of data and infrastructure.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** etl (1), elt (1)

#### Data scientists
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=0)** - People often pursue data with the hopes of becoming a data scientist.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=4)** And I believe it's important to know that not all data professionals grow into data scientists, nor do we need all analysts or engineers to turn into data scientists.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=14)** Data scientists will likely have all the skills of the analyst engineer and they will have likely worked in those roles.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=21)** However, a data scientist will have a heavier requirement for skills in coding, mathematics, and statistics.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=27)** A data scientist will be instrumental in developing tools and instruments that provide valuable insight to the organization, but they can't do it alone without all the other roles, or well, maybe they can perform the task, but when you don't have all the other roles, the data scientists must perform them.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=46)** Data scientists or data science teams comprised of all the disciplines will interpret large sets.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=52)** They'll likely build machine learning models.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=55)** They'll present outcomes and make suggestions as a portion of what they do.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=59)** They'll likely be leaders in the data science team.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=62)** They'll provide support and strategy to the overall data governance plan.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=66)** If you want to further your skills in this area, you should consider gaining a better understanding of programmatic thinking.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=73)** You'll want to dive deeper into learning code and maybe start with something like Python.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=78)** If you have some stats experience, or not, you will definitely want to grow in this area.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=83)** Remember, one of the key differences between data scientists and all other roles is heavier math, coding, and stats.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=90)** It's also important to remember that for most organizations, having a data scientist and not having all the other roles means that that data scientist is having to perform all those roles before they get to the data science.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-career-skills-in-data-analytics/data-scientists?u=76281980&t=104)** This is where having a team of multi-discipline people serving all the roles might just be your next play.
